I have made this about 30 times since finding this recipe...I SOOOO should have posted this rating sooner. This was FANTASTIC...I noticed the last two people rated this with ONE star and they must be crazy or not experienced with baking. I bake almost every day...for the past 10 years and this is BY FAR the best pound cake recipe I have found yet. It is moist, tasty fluffy and flavourful....I think I baked it in less time, but I prefer things baked with a lower temp and less time...just a personal preference. I took it out as soon as the center seemed remotely cooked and left it on the counter for about an hour before attempting cutting it. It was soooo good. My hubby and kids ate a whole one that night and my hubby took another to work the next day and got rave reviews from it. This is the only pound cake I have made since finding this recipe and it will of course be the last...we have found a winner!!! SOOO tasty and moist. I have made this recipe as is about 25 times and a few times I made it with berries or apples or just with cinnamon. Its sooo good the way the recipe intended, but also good once in awhile with berries. Thanks soooooo so much for posting this recipe. Its definately a keeper.

An excellent recipe and a true pound cake, where you use an actual pound of each ingrediant. I reject any recipe that does not have a pound of butter in it. Those cakes are good, but not true poundcakes. I've become a poundcake snob. LOL!

I add some lemon zest, or a full two teaspoons of vanilla extract sometimes. I've also been known to trade the sweet milk, for buttermilk. 

I've made this and the other Grandmother's poundcake from this site over and over and will not use any other recipes for my pound cake.

I think the individuals that posted bad reviews have no concept of what pound cake is. If you're used to Sara Lee or Entenman's, don't bother. Real pound cake got it's name because you are supposed to use a pound of each ingredient. The result should be a very dense cake. Of course, you have to be careful not to overbake or you'll end up with something too dry!

text:
I took the following suggestions from the invaluable reviews: 1. Add a tablespoon of vanilla. 2. Replace 1 cup of white sugar with 1 cup of brown sugar. 3. Beat the butter and sugar for 5 minutes, and then for another minute as each egg is added. I also beat for a minute after adding the vanilla (which I do after the eggs). Result: A gorgeous, dense, flavorful, buttery cake with a crisp brown crust. For those who like Sara Lee pound cake (and I do) this creates a very similar flavor. Fantastic cake.

text:
Yes, this is the formula for a classic American pound cake as it has been made for well over a century and a half (1:1:1:1 or 1 pound butter, 1 pound sugar, 1 pound flour, 1 pound eggs.) I used this as a base for petits fours, and the texture stood up to repeated cuts (I halved the recipe, and baked in a 9"X13" pan, then cut 7X10 into (70) 1-1/4" squares) and didn't shed crumbs, neither when it was cut, nor when the fondant was poured over it. I did, however, add more milk. This was so short on liquid that the result was closer to a dough than a batter. I added 50% more milk, and added extracts (combo of almond, vanilla, orange, lemon , maple and coconut) as I needed the cake to have sufficiently assertive and complex flavor to stand up to the uber sweet fondant. The 9"X13" was done in 27 minutes. I cooled it in the pan for about 13 minutes, and it released beautifully onto the rack to finish. This cake is appropriately dense, sturdy and velvety moist (with additional liquid.) It's a 4-1/2 star recipe as is, but a 5 with additional milk and flavoring, which yields distinct sensory improvement.

made this real pound cake again today. I dont understand the one star ratings this recipe is getting. you absolutely MUST beat the softened butter and sugar for more then five minutes with a good mixer. more like ten minutes. beat that mix like it owes you money. add the eggs one at a time. add your flavorings before the flour. remembering to subtract that liquid amount from the milk amount. add the flour and mix JUST UNTIL its blended in. I made a lemon bundt pound cake today. i used 1 and 1/2 juice and rind of regular lemons. added vanilla also. I only needed small amount of milk. im goin to glaze this deliciousness with lemon glaze and serve it for thanksgiving dessert.

Perfect! I looked at over 30 pound cake recipes, but being a purist, chose this- so glad I did.

text:
Excellent! I think the key to getting a cake with great texture is to make sure that ALL of your ingredients are at room temp before you start. Pre-measure your milk, take your eggs and butter out (it helps to cut your butter up into small cubes before you use your mixer), but yes, take everything out at least 30 mins before you start. Also, be sure to beat at a medium-high speed, rather than a low speed. The batter should be super smooth (no lumps) when you're all done. And it's a bit thicker than regular cake batter too- sorta like frosting at room temp, or maybe just a hair softer. I thought that I had over mixed mine, it was incredibly light and fluffy, but it came out PERFECT and I mixed for a long time in between eggs and milk/flour. I don't think I'll have to worry about over mixing next time. The only modification I made to the recipe was that I added 2tsp of PURE vanilla extract and 2 tsp of almond extract. I could have gotten away with just one of each, or even none at all, it's a tad sweet, but still yummy as ever. 
Great recipe! It took awhile to find a classic pound cake recipe- I am very pleased:)

text:
This recipe was exactly what I was looking for! It's just like the pound cake my mom made when I was small--not too sweet, very dense and moist, and a nice, sugary crust on top.  Two things: I was alarmed when I was finished mixing the batter and the instructions read to pour it into the pan, because my batter was so thick I had to spoon it in and level it with a rubber spatula. So, don't worry if your batter seems thick. Also, since I halved the recipe and used a 9.25 x 5.25 loaf pan, I only had enough batter to fill the pan a little over halfway. The cake didn't rise much, which is not a bad thing at all, but the final shape of my cake was kind of funny, flat loaf. (My fault entirely!) Next time I'll use smaller pans, and whatever the size, make sure I fill them 3/4 full.  Great recipe, thanks for sharing!

text:
This is a great pound cake recipe!!! You have to remember, since there is no leavening in a traditional pound cake, YOU (the baker) have to provide the leavening by creaming the ingredients appropriately and beating each egg in one by one. Doing this incorporates air into the batter, which is what helps the eggs to their job in leavening. Cream the butter and sugar for a minimum of 5 minutes, if not longer. It should increase in volume and turn white and fluffy, looking a lot like whipped heavy cream. Beat each egg in for about a minute before adding another egg (yes, watch the clock...a minute can be longer than you think!). I added a dash of salt because I didn't use salted butter (there is a dairy allergy in the house so I used shortening instead of butter), added a Tbsp of vanilla extract, and I used rice milk in place of dairy milk (again, the dairy allergy thing). Perfect!!! Good, old fashioned pound cake.

AWESOME.  An elderly lady once told me that CREAMING means that when you rub it between your fingers there are no sugar crystals.  It takes 15-20 minutes if you have a great mixer.  Be patient.  This did not need anything at all but was incredible as strawberry shortcake.  I followed another reviewer's recommendation and baked in a bundt pan @350 for 50 minutes.  I had enough for a small loaf pan as well.  It does not rise much but I didn't want it to overflow.  It makes ALOT of cake...  My grandma owned a bakery where she used pound cake cut in 1x2x3(or height of cake), roled in a runny frosting, and then rolled in crushed salted peanuts.  She called it a salted nut roll and I am looking forward to that as soon as I get some peanuts.  YUM.

Love it! This is way better than any store bought pound cake! I added pure vanilla extract & a small spoonful of sour cream to mine, it turned out great! Now I can see why maybe a few people gave this recipe bad reviews, if you eat this right out of the hot oven, it doesn't taste so great hot. It needs time to settle & cool. text:
This is one of the rare recipes that needs no adjustments.   I have made it several times exactly as written, and it's perfect every time.  It even bakes in the amount of time called for.  I generally have bad luck with cakes from scratch; this one works like a charm.  It's good plain or in a trifle or shortcake.  My husband's favorite way to eat this is to butter and grill it, then serve it with Chef John's strawberry sauce.  Do use real butter.  When you have so so few ingredients, you have to use the real thing.  Normally I use shortening in cookies and pie crusts, but butter makes this cake stand out.  Happy baking!

text:
I suspect the people who had trouble with this recipe don't really know what "light and fluffy" means when it comes to the butter and sugar part.  You really have to beat it for a long time. Very soft butter, 4-6 mins. Semi-soft butter, 5-8 mins. If you're a novice baker, this is an easy mistake to make. Most other things don't need you butter and sugar beaten this much. 
Also, when mixing the milk and flour alternately, make sure you start and finish with flour. If you finish with milk, the texture looks off and it might cause you to over-mix.

I followed the recipe exactly, changing nothing, except I did add vanilla flavoring, and adjusted the amount of milk to reflect that, so the liquid measurement wouldn't be changed. All of my ingredients were at room temperature. I used a Kitchen Aid stand mixer to do all the considerable beating required. Eggs went in one at a time, beating at least 90 seconds before adding the next. The batter was lovely, very fluffy and pale yellow, like I remember my grandmother making. (I was so excited over that! She made amazing pound cakes!)  I greased &  lined the loaf pans, put the batter in and set the loaves baking at 350. When they  were done they looked beautiful, just like my grandmother's. The outer crust looked perfect, that little split in the top crust was there. I put them on cooling racks. When they cooled I cut my husband a slice. There was this greasy line near the bottom of each cake, where it appears butter settled. The cake itself had a nice texture but a bit heavy and was very very eggy tasting. I couldn't taste the vanilla flavoring at all, and I added a tablespoon of that. Overall I'm so disappointed. I had hoped to give two of the cakes as thank you gifts in a basket of goodies, but I'm thinking now I'll make cookies instead. 
I don't know what went wrong, but all three loaves had that identical oily looking streak near the bottom. I know my oven temp is spot on, I baked for the time stated in the recipe. I can't figure out what caused it. I've never had this issu

I made this cake for my father's birthday. He always mentions how much he loves the traditional pound cake with no glaze or frosting. And I'm so glad that I've tried this recipe!
The batter was more than enough for one bundt cake pan, so i made mini cupcakes of the remaining batter.
I've tried making pound cakes before, never liked any of them. This one is more than amazing!
But to my taste, I added 3 teaspoons of vanilla extract and substituted heavy whipping cream with milk. I found the batter to be so dense so I followed one of the reviews here and added 1 cup and 3 tablespoons of the whipping cream. 
The result is amazing  more than I've imagined.
Thank you for this recipe! Will definitely make again!

text:
Sorry, but I really have to question the one-star reviews; maybe they were just expecting something different? Because honestly, I think you'd have to try to mess up this recipe. I actually only made this cake so that I could take pictures of it for a project, so I wasn't terribly invested in the end product- in fact, I only chose pound cake because it required the fewest ingredients and, therefore, no grocery run. I cut the recipe down to one third, I rounded measurements, and my rarely-used loaf pan turned out to be bigger than I thought, so I ended up with an odd, flat loaf. My butter and eggs were cold, and I probably could have beaten everything a litte more thoroughly. The point? This cake is STILL pretty darn good. Would I bring it to a party? Probably not, but it won't last long around my husband and me. And considering how I tortured it, imagine how good it would be done right. For what it's worth, I did add a tablespoon of vanilla, and took it out after 40 minutes because my single, squashed little loaf was looking a bit brown around the edges - probably would've been perfect at around 35 minutes.

WOW!! This is the best pound cake I have ever made.  It is so moist and delicious.  The only problem I had was I put the batter in two 9x5 pans and that made too much.  Took to long to bake and the top got a littlt too done, but other than that this recipe is GREAT. I added two teaspoons of vanilla, but I might use coconut next time.  Thanks for sharing this recipe.

text:
As is, the cake turned out dry so I overhauled it for my taste. Reduced the flour to 3 cups, used 1 cup of sour cream instead of milk.  I added 4 t vanilla and 1/4 t baking soda. I separated the eggs and dropped in the yokes one at a time. I whipped up the egg whites until stiff peaks formed and folded the egg whites into the cake batter just before pouring into the bundt pan.  The cake came out fabulous and I keep getting asked to make it again and again.  Thank grandmother for her great base recipe.

country:

text:
I want to say 1st that I do not like pound cake!!! I made it for my God mother because she requested one and I like to back. I came on this website searching for a repicie and I chose this one. I read all the reviews and after a few alterations, this cake was delicious even for me. My alterations were: I preheated my oven to 325 degrees. I used 2 loaf pans instead of a bundt pan. Eggs and butter must be room temperature! I used one cup of brown sugar and 2 cups of white and creamed with the butter for literally 20min ( I set a timer). Add one egg at a time, 1 min apart. I used 1/2 tablespoon of pure vanilla and 1/2 tablespoon of almond extract. I also put in 1/4 tablespoon of lemon extract. I used cake flour instead of all purpose flour and sifted 3 times before adding in with heavy whipping cream instead of milk. I baked for about an hour.  I waited until it completely cooled.  Cake came out light brown, full flavored, and delicious.

text:
This is the best pound cake recipe ever! I followed it almost exactly. I used half brown sugar half white sugar and an extra teaspoon of vanilla. I also made a brown sugar pineapple mixture and placed it in the bottom of the bread pans. It turned out amazing! I will make this for sure again. A note to those who think this recipe doesn't turn out, there is gluten in flour and when you overmix it, it becomes rubbery. The 5 minute mixing is meant for before you put in the flower. I mixed for five minutes before adding eggs. I then mixed for one minute after each egg then only mixed long enough to incorporate the flower by each cup.

This cake was ok.   Ill probably just keep looking and try a true pound cake, which is a pound of each ingredient  (a pound of sugar is about 2 cups, not 3; a pound of eggs is about 8; no milk should be added). I did add a tablespoon of vanilla. Itd be pretty bland without it. Also, a recipe I used (and lost) a long time ago said to beat the sugar and butter together for about 10 minutes, because you want the sugar crystals to dissolve, to give it a better texture. I did do that.

text:
I keep making this .... I don't know how many times -- I shouldn't eat a lot of carbs, so I tend to gift these.  The only change I made, is I stir in a half-teaspoon of double-strength vanilla  with the milk because I love the aroma of vanilla (I use Penzey's as it's not half-artificial like other double-strength vanillas tend to be).  I have nice ceramic loaf pans that work really well.  The key is having all the ingredients at room temperature.  Use the highest quality ingredients you can afford -- if that's the uncut pound of store-brand butter, it's still tasty, but this is a recipe where all the ingredients shine because it's so basic and has so few ingredients.  If you can pay the tariff on Euro or Irish butter, then go for it.  Same for farmers' market eggs.

text:
A critical instruction is missing from Step 2. The butter, sugar and eggs must be beat for a good ten minutes. If you mix until just incorporated youll end up with a dense bread-like lump, resulting in a 1 or 2 star result. I mix butter and sugar for 7 minutes and then 1 egg at a time, allowing about 1 1/2 minutes between each egg addition. Magicthe difference between barely passable & outstanding.

text:
For those who want success with any pound cake:  First of all, the ingredients need to be at room temperature.

Beat the butter alone for a good five minutes and gradually add in the sugar. No shortcuts on time here! You want it to be thoroughly incorporated. Add the eggs, one at a time, and again, beat well. Repeat. I've always added in the flavorings next, beat well, and then the milk, beat well. Then slowly add in the flour. You should end up with a very smooth, silky and thick batter. Spoon it into your prepared pans and bake.

text:
I love pound cake, and after trying a few recipes with disappointing results, I come back most often to this one. I gave it 5 stars because it's an excellent base cake and can be tweaked to perfection according to taste. Not to be one of those people who are like, "I loved it! I changed half the ingredients," but this is how I make it, with stellar results. I love a buttery cake with a hint of salt to offset the sweetness of the sugar, and this hits the spot.

I make a half recipe and put it in a sculpted Bundt pan, which fills about 2/3 of the pan. I use cream instead of milk. I add 1 tsp salt (so if you're making a full recipe, make it 2 tsp). I add 1 Tbsp of vanilla (again, double for a full recipe). I have also made this with a tablespoon of orange zest, or lemon zest (either one is great! you get a beautiful light citrus flavor), or 1/3 cup of chocolate chips.

If you're using a Bundt pan, bake for 45-55 minutes. My oven runs a little cool, so I test at 50 minutes and then go for the extra 5 if needed, which creates a glorious brown crust on the cake. Then, let the cake cool on the oven top for 10-15 minutes, then bang it hard against the floor several times to get the cake to release from the sides of the pan. You can let it cool for another 10 minutes or so if you wish, then turn it out of the pan.

Another secret: wrap the WARM cake tightly in Saran Wrap. No, this will not make your cake soggy. It seems like that's what would happen, but it doesn't. It seals in all th

I'm rating the recipe 5* because the cake itself  is great, exactly as written.  (pound cake batter is always thick, and it does not require additional liquid to thin it out).   However, I made the mistake of pouring all the batter into a large bunt pan, layering as I went with maraschino cherries, and that was a mistake.  The outside of the cake cooked faster than the inside did so the outside was dry and the inside gluey. :(  Next time I will either make 1/2 the recipe or I will use 2 or possibly 3 loaf pans to ensure even cooking.

This is a true pound cake, dense, moist, and delicious. For added flavor, I added a tablespoon of vanilla and a tsp of almond extract. Be aware that almond extract is a very strong flavor. I wish I had added less, but this pound cake was delicious nonetheless. It has a crunchy outer layer  with a moist interior. As noted in other ratings, the batter is quite thick, so "pouring"  the batter into prepared pans is not quite an accurate term. I "scooped" it into the pans.  I ended up with extra batter, which I baked into muffins. Excellent recipe!!

text:
This was SOOOOO yummy!! I made it exactly as written, but adjusted the amounts to only make 2 loaves, and it came out so great great they were both gone in less than 24 hours!  I will say that you definitely have to make sure you beat the butter and sugar until very light and fluffy, and do not skip the adding only one egg at a time. It might not seem like a big deal, but since there is nothing else to make this cake rise, you MUST beat everything very well before you add the flour. Once you're adding the flour, don't overbeat it or, again, it won't rise correctly. I always make a recipe by the directions the first time, and it is awesome, but I'm sure it would be great with vanilla,lemon, or almond extract added. Yum!!

text:
This is a good base recipe but I think it needs to be a little more specific! My first attempt came out badly (rubbery and crumbly) but I researched some baking tips for pound cake online and the second came out perfect! 

Use unsalted butter (you can add salt to your taste if you'd like). Make sure all wet ingredients (eggs, milk, and butter) are room temperature. Make sure the butter is softened (not melted or still hard!). Add the 1/3 of the flour to the sugar/eggs/butter, mix, then 1/2 the milk, mix, then 1/3 of the flour again, mix, then the rest of the milk, mix, then add the last of flour. When mixing (I used a hand mixer), total mixing time should only be 3-5 minutes.

The reason why cakes turn out rubbery or crumbly is because it is overmixed (which is what I did the first attempt). Also you need to let it cool before taking it out of the pan or else it will turn even more crumbly. 

I hope this helps!

This was my first time ever making pound cake- I used to make a trifle with bananas, pastry cream, whipped cream and vanilla wafer crumbs.  

I creamed the butter for a couple min on med speed, then added the sugar and creamed it for a few more min.  I added the eggs 1 at a time, beating well after each addition. It can be a little deceiving because it looked gooey in the middle still but I should have taken it out about 10 min sooner. text:
I made this recipe exactly as instructed, except that I added 3 tsp of vanilla extract and 2 tsp almond extract.  Even with all that flavoring, it tasted somewhat bland.  I'm not sure why all these reviews say that you need to beat the daylights out of the batter--the recipes says no such thing and actually cautions against over-beating in the final stages.  I wish I had ignored the reviewers and spent less time beating this batter.  The cake came out much, much too fluffy for a pound cake, which should be denser.  Otherwise, the texture was very nice.  I ended up having to frost it for the sake of flavor.  I might make it again, but with a lot less beating and a fruit compote to drizzle on top.

text:
I used a scale to measure 1 pound each of flour, sugar, and egg. In my experiment, I used extra large eggs, and got 1.08 pounds from 8 eggs, after removing the shells.

I substituted lemon juice for the milk to make a lemon pound cake. The dough was liquidy enough to flow in the bowl, but when I poured it into the pans, it broke off in pieces just past the rim. The result was far superior to pound cakes that skimp on butter, or eggs. For my personal not-too-sweet-please tooth, the sugar was a little much, but not so much that I would deprive others of it.

Oh this is the best cake! Perfect for gift giving too. I added a few things to make it original. I added 1 tsp salt, 1 Tblsp lemon extract, 2 Tblsp vanilla extract, & 1 tsp coconut extract. If I had almond extract on hand I would have added 1 tsp almond extract. BAKING change too. Grease Bundy pan with Crisco butter & flour lightly. Set  Oven temp 325 degrees bake cake for 90 minutes(1&1/2 hrs.) To not burn cake & soon as it cones out the oven place serving plate on top of bundt pan & flip it as it slides right out of cake. Easy cleanup too.

text:
I tried this recipe yesterday but I cut the ingredients in half because I only wanted one 9x5 loaf pan sized cake. Went together really easy and baked up nice and full but at 350 for 70 minutes it burnt around the edges. Could be the new loaf pan I used because it's a dark metal one or maybe I need to bake it at 325 instead. We haven't tasted it yet but it seemed kind of dry when I cut it in half to wrap it but I know that was because it was over baked. Anyway next time I'll try turning the oven down to 325 and just watching and testing until it's fully baked so I don't burn the edges again. I'm rating it 5 stars just because it goes together so quickly and easily and has so few ingredients. The over baking was my own fault since I was using a new pan and halving the recipe and then not watching it close enough. We're going to use it for strawberry shortcake so I'm sure the juice from the berries and whipped cream will make it more than edible.

photo:
https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5674169.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is definitely true pound cake.  Came out nice and dense, and perfectly browned.  My oven always seems to take longer on baking, so I baked mine for about 1 1/4 hours.  I also followed the reviews and added 1 1/2 tsp of powdered vanilla.  (I could have added more, it would have taken it nicely).  I mixed the butter and sugar for a loooong time in the food processor ( I don't have a hand mixer) until it was super smooth, then made sure not to overmix when adding the eggs, and finally, I poured everything into a mixing bowl and used a hand whisk to add the flour and milk.  I think it made a world of difference in the texture, so for those who are having texture problems, try it.  The key is to not incorporate too much air after adding the eggs.  Thanks for such an authentic recipe :-D

If I make it again, I'd bake it for maybe 45-50 minutes.
